  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0803dd1c-c1f3-4d51-8879-f920463ec398'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer6300912595382929061"><b>From #1 New York Times bestselling author Brandon Sanderson, the Mistborn series is a heist story of political intrigue and magical, martial-arts action. </b><br/><br/>Three hundred years after the events of the Mistborn trilogy, Scadrial is now on the verge of modernity, with railroads to supplement the canals, electric lighting in the streets and the homes of the wealthy, and the firs</span>
  <span id="freeText6300912595382929061" style="display:none"><b>From #1 New York Times bestselling author Brandon Sanderson, the Mistborn series is a heist story of political intrigue and magical, martial-arts action. </b><br /><br />Three hundred years after the events of the Mistborn trilogy, Scadrial is now on the verge of modernity, with railroads to supplement the canals, electric lighting in the streets and the homes of the wealthy, and the first steel-framed skyscrapers racing for the clouds.<br /><br />The Bands of Mourning are the mythical metal minds owned by the Lord Ruler, said to grant anyone who wears them the powers that the Lord Ruler had at his command. Hardly anyone thinks they really exist. A kandra researcher has returned to Elendel with images that seem to depict the Bands, as well as writings in a language that no one can read. Waxillium Ladrian is recruited to travel south to the city of New Seran to investigate. Along the way he discovers hints that point to the true goals of his uncle Edwarn and the shadowy organization known as The Set.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6300912595382929061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/585907-how-is-this-series-compared-to-mistborn">how is this series compared to Mistborn?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_585907'><a id="like_count_community_question_585907" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/585907?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">7 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18739426-the-bands-of-mourning">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/3274968-nikki"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1464797286i/3274968._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/3274968-nikki">Nikki</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This series is different from the original trilogy, for sure. It has more of a "western" vibe. But it still has all the charms of the original trilogy<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This series is different from the original trilogy, for sure. It has more of a "western" vibe. But it still has all the charms of the original trilogy -- great characters, same magic system (but it's evolving!), fantastic worldbuilding, and great plots (though more crime-fighting-ish and less of the high-fantasy world-saving variety). <br /><br />I wanted to correct an earlier answer, though: The Alloy of Law isn't (technically) part of the Alloy-era trilogy. AoL starts the Alloy-era arc, but the official trilogy is Shadows of Self, The Bands of Mourning (Jan 2016), and The Lost Metal (2017). There are two more Mistborn trilogies to come after this one: one set in a time similar to the 1980s, and a far-future 'space opera'-type trilogy (with travel between planets). :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1745130507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1745130507" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745130507?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473208254" href="/book/show/24734047-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745130507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10039443139619796447">Did I just fall in love with an organisation freak named Steris? <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473337246ra/20449187.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Seriously though, her character really shines through in this book. Before she just seemed a bit dull, and perhaps even ordinary, but this clearly isn’t the case. She is an exceptional woman, one who is clearly overlooked and dramatically undervalued by all that meet her. Behind her stoic appearance and general aura of nonchalance is a woman who is slightly obsessive to a fault; however, she is also fiercely loyal to her friends an</span>
  <span id="freeText10039443139619796447" style="display:none">Did I just fall in love with an organisation freak named Steris? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473337246ra/20449187.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously though, her character really shines through in this book. Before she just seemed a bit dull, and perhaps even ordinary, but this clearly isn’t the case. She is an exceptional woman, one who is clearly overlooked and dramatically undervalued by all that meet her. Behind her stoic appearance and general aura of nonchalance is a woman who is slightly obsessive to a fault; however, she is also fiercely loyal to her friends and family. She is the sort of person you simply want on your side in a conflict.<br><br>So this book, for me, was all about her. Sure Wax goes on another exciting adventure, but this was Steris’ breakout book if you like: it was the book in which the true nature of her character was revealed. She reminded me somewhat of a librarian or an archivist, a person who has been shut away from reality for some time and is finally having to face it. She’s clumsy and awkward. She’s inexperienced and a minor liability, though she is also brave and willing to adapt. She doesn’t want to be left behind, and she is willing to become something more to insure that this doesn’t become the case. And you really have to respect her for it. She’s a great character. For me, there wasn’t much else in this book. <br><br>Postscript- I couldn’t help picturing her as Evelyne from the mummy hence the gif at the start!<br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/sean.barrs" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>| <a href="https://twitter.com/ultra_vegan" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>| <a href="https://www.instagram.com/sean.ultra_vegan/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Insta</a>| <a href="https://york.academia.edu/SeanBarrs" rel="nofollow noopener">Academia</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10039443139619796447" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_952044008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952044008" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/952044008?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bro-mantic">bro-mantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer952044008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2310702204872507938"><b>4.75 Investiture Filled Stars</b><br/><br/>Buddy read with my friends at <a>Buddies Books & Baubles</a> the discussion is still ongoing but I had to know all the things.<br/><br/><i>Spoiler Free Review Section:</i><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>There is always another secret<i></i></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>How many times have we read those very words throughout the Mistborn saga and been shown yet again that there IS definitely always another secret. Brandon Sanderson has proved that once again in Bands of Mourning. <i>I know who this is about now and I am OMG excited</i><br/><br/><b>First </b> he surprised</span>
  <span id="freeText2310702204872507938" style="display:none"><b>4.75 Investiture Filled Stars</b><br><br>Buddy read with my friends at <a>Buddies Books &amp; Baubles</a> the discussion is still ongoing but I had to know all the things.<br><br><i>Spoiler Free Review Section:</i><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>There is always another secret<i></i></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>How many times have we read those very words throughout the Mistborn saga and been shown yet again that there IS definitely always another secret. Brandon Sanderson has proved that once again in Bands of Mourning. <i>I know who this is about now and I am OMG excited</i><br><br><b>First </b> he surprised all his fans by revealing that he had a secret project with ended up being a novella set in the time of the first 3 Mistborn with a beloved character. But don’t read it until after Bands of Mourning because there will be some spoilers. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036.Mistborn_Secret_History__Mistborn___6_5_" title="Mistborn Secret History (Mistborn, #6.5) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a><br><br><b>Second</b> there is the actual book Bands of Mourning which if you are an allomancy/Feruchemy/Hemilurgy nerd like I can be there are new ways of combining metals/powers for cool effects. But with the introduction of Investiture a whole new realm of possibilities opens up and that is the focus of this book. What if you could store allomantic or Feruchemical powers and anyone could use them. The Lord Rulers Bands of Mourning are thought to hold this type of power. The ways that BS explores this new concept hit me right out left field I didn’t expect the story to go that direction but man what a ride.<br><br><b>Third</b> after what Wax went through in Shadows of Self how do you come to terms with your god and the role he chose for you. Wax’s anger is palpable and coming to terms with the events from SoS plays a large role in some of the decisions he is making. But it is hard to avoid Gods plans when he has walking talking emissaries that show up and maneuver you into helping.<br><br><b>Then</b> there are all the great character interactions. I love the bromance between Wax and Wayne how they have something of their own language and know each other so well but at the same time are so different. <br><br>Wayne is one of my favorite characters in literature as he has his own special brand of logic and way of looking at the world that is somewhat ridiculous at times but always entertaining, unique and full of funny. <br><blockquote>
  <i>”…At the precinct, when I accomplish something, everyone assumes I had Waxillium’s help. Sometimes it’s like I’m no more than an appendage.”<br>“You’re not that at all, Marasi,” Wayne said. “You’re important. You help out a lot. Plus you smell nice, and not all bloody and stuff.”<br>“Great. I have no idea what you just said.”<br>“Appendages don’t smell nice,” Wayne said. “And they’re kinda gross. I cut one outta a fellow once.”<br><b>“You mean an appendix?”<br>“Sure.” He hesitated.<br>“So…” “Not the same thing.”<br>“Right. Thought you was makin’ a metaphor, since people don’t need one of those and all.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Steris also has become one of my favorite characters in the series. While really pretty stiff and mostly absent in Alloy of Law she has come a long way. Steris was my most improved character in Shadows of Self and in Bands of Mourning she really continues to charm me with her lists, wonder and overthinking of every situation. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“Is that the constables?” Aunt Gin asked, sounding horrified. <br>“Afraid so,” Wax said, pulling the door closed. The carriage lurched into motion, and Steris leaned out the window, waving farewell to the poor innkeeper.<br><b>“Framed for murder!” Steris called to her. “It’s on page seventeen of the list I gave you!</b> Try not to let them harass our servants too much when they arrive!”</i>
</blockquote><br>But somehow as Wax has come to care about her more so have I and it is official I have changed ships and actually love Wax and Steris for each other now. <i>Don’t judge me, it was hard I’m always super loyal to the first love interest</i><br><br><b>Finally</b> - New places and new people! Venturing out of Elendale to another city and getting a different perspective on the both the people of Elendale and those in the cities surrounding Elendale gave a new depth to this world and the political issues in it. <b>AND THEN</b> there are the other people with MASKS…..<i>runs away and hides</i> I’ll totally talk about them in the spoiler section of the review. Let’s just say that they are a game changer to this series I think<br><br><b>Spoiler Section of this review is Under Construciton</b><br><br>Oh I have much to say….so it will be a few days after I calm down and think through some things.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453936374i/17893195._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2310702204872507938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review952044008">

<div id="review_1880227738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1880227738" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1880227738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2364908345752572947">So here we are. <b>Here we are.</b><br/><br/>I just don't know <i>how much more praise</i> I can shower on Brandon Sanderson's <i>Mistborn</i> series before people start questioning whether or not I'm in a cult...<br/><br/>ಠ_ಠ<br/><br/>This book was <u>my favorite</u> of the second era <i>Mistborn</i> series. The characters go through some wonderful developments, and I'm <b>fascinated</b> by this mix of Fantasy elements with a Western setting.<br/><br/>I feel like Bands of Mourning works particularly well because by this point we are already very well acquainted with the magi</span>
  <span id="freeText2364908345752572947" style="display:none">So here we are. <b>Here we are.</b><br><br>I just don't know <i>how much more praise</i> I can shower on Brandon Sanderson's <i>Mistborn</i> series before people start questioning whether or not I'm in a cult...<br><br>ಠ_ಠ<br><br>This book was <u>my favorite</u> of the second era <i>Mistborn</i> series. The characters go through some wonderful developments, and I'm <b>fascinated</b> by this mix of Fantasy elements with a Western setting.<br><br>I feel like Bands of Mourning works particularly well because by this point we are already very well acquainted with the magic systems, and we've warmed up to our new cast of characters. <br><br>So reading this, you're experiencing all the <b>wonder &amp; excitement</b> of a brand new adventure while feeling <b>cozy &amp; comfortable</b> beneath a heavy blanket of nostalgia. <br><br><b>
  <i>This has been one of my favorite reading journeys I've ever taken. <u>EVER.</u></i>
</b><br><br>Reading it with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7317186-celeste" rel="nofollow noopener">Celeste</a> just made the experience all that more memorable!<br><br>I'm not gonna lie, I'm pretty messed up right now thinking about how long I will have to wait to continue this series. <u>But I'm forever grateful for its existence.</u><br><br>Please enjoy this actual footage of me while I wait:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487733514ra/22045531.gif" width="500" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1604182363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1604182363" />
    <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna"><img alt="Lady Luna. ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575639837p2/53385361.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=great-books">great-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=written-by-the-hand-of-god">written-by-the-hand-of-god</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=flintlock-fantasy">flintlock-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1604182363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4335805626395512045">5 MIND BLOWN STARS ★★★★★<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He’s the man who takes the bullet so nobody else has to.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483609375i/21629807._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>HOW FUCKING DARE THIS BOOK BE SO BLOODY AMAZING! </b>Seriously.. That ending holy fucking shit. This book has left me breathless... like wow! So different to anything I've read by Sanderson but it was incredible and is my favourite of all six Mistborn books! This book felt different from the first page, it was so fucking exciting and I knew straight away it was building up to a massive ending.. I'm gobsmac</span>
  <span id="freeText4335805626395512045" style="display:none">5 MIND BLOWN STARS ★★★★★<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He’s the man who takes the bullet so nobody else has to.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483609375i/21629807._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>HOW FUCKING DARE THIS BOOK BE SO BLOODY AMAZING! </b>Seriously.. That ending holy fucking shit. This book has left me breathless... like wow! So different to anything I've read by Sanderson but it was incredible and is my favourite of all six Mistborn books! This book felt different from the first page, it was so fucking exciting and I knew straight away it was building up to a massive ending.. I'm gobsmacked. This is the hardest book I've ever had to review, how can you review such perfection? <br>I've been waiting for this book for my whole existence.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Do you ever wonder if perhaps the cosmere is out to overwhelm you, Lord Waxillium?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I'm convinced Sanderson is not a human being. How does his brain think of such complex plots, how can a human write so many books in the one universe and have them all connected in some way. How does he manage to blow my mind in every single book? My conclusion is he is an alien who has cloned himself to write so fast. I love Brandon Sanderson so much and this book has just confirmed to me that he is the King of fantasy. <b>I swear if your not a fan then I hate you.</b><br><br>So basically this book follows Wax &amp; Wayne again, they and Marasi are sent on a secret mission. Steris comes along with them and finally gets some decent page space. A lot of questions are answered. I also noticed a certain someone posing as a beggar. It also has the best fight on a train with guns scene, that was absolutely epic and that ending was ridiculous (in a good way). I got Biosock vibes.<br><br>The character growth for everyone was amazing and the bromance between Wax &amp; Wayne is one of my favourites. Wax is just so dreamy, you see a much softer side to him in this book. But he is still tough, badass &amp; the most awesome character ever. He is just incredible he is a superhero. And i finally got my ship! Yay.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Cod-liver oil and metal flakes washed into his mouth. Swallowing took a precious moment.<br>Nothing.<br>Nothing.<br>Nothing.<br>Power.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483609814i/21629845._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>^^ I love these covers so much. Wax is just perfect.<br><br>Wayne's character was less like able for me in this book for some reason. He still made me laugh and stuff but something was off about him. He did however have some badass moments.<br><br>I've always loved steris so I was happy for her to get more page space&amp; shine like the gem she is her personality is amazing. I adore her. She's one of my favorite female characters ever.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483609375i/21629808._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Since when have you carried one of these?” Wax asked, taking it from her.<br>“Since about six months ago. I put one into my purse in case you might need it.” She raised her other hand, displaying two more. “I carry the other two because I’m neurotic.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Marasi actually is slowly wearing on me, I found her much more tolerable in this book. But she's still annoying.<br><br><b>Bring on book seven I need it now. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453635634ra/17852060.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <b>“Please ignore him,” Steris said, rising and walking over. “Here, I’ve prepared for you a list of possible scenarios that might transpire during our residence here.”<br>“Steris…” Wax said, forcing open the third and final window.<br>“What?” she demanded. “I will not have the staff unprepared. Their safety is our concern.”<br>“Fire?” Aunt Gin asked, reading the list. “Shoot-outs. Robbery. Hostage situations. Explosions?”<br>“That one is completely unfair,” Wax said. “You’ve been listening to Wayne.”<br>“Things do explode around you, mate,” Wayne said, munching peanuts.”</b>
</i></span>

<div id="review_2137854729" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137854729" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137854729?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473208278" href="/book/show/26541448-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137854729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15618864054048703133">Honestly, I do not know how to review these books. This book. This spin-off series. It's not that I have been rendered speechless. It's just slightly difficult, mainly when it comes to the plot. So, I'll try to break it down into sections. It will be more of a series review, rather than focusing on The Bands of Mourning alone. <br/><br/><b>Plot/world-building:</b><br/>This I will say went slightly over my head, especially as the books progressed. Each time I thought I had a grasp of it, a different point connecting t</span>
  <span id="freeText15618864054048703133" style="display:none">Honestly, I do not know how to review these books. This book. This spin-off series. It's not that I have been rendered speechless. It's just slightly difficult, mainly when it comes to the plot. So, I'll try to break it down into sections. It will be more of a series review, rather than focusing on The Bands of Mourning alone. <br /><br /><b>Plot/world-building:</b><br />This I will say went slightly over my head, especially as the books progressed. Each time I thought I had a grasp of it, a different point connecting to the plot would be mentioned and I'd be lost again. It's the main reason why I couldn't give these books 5 stars and it's more of a fault on my own rather than Sanderson. Can't fault Sanderson. Borders blasphemy, let's get real here.<br />It is something that I know would become clearer for me when I do decide to reread them though.<br /><br />But in true Sanderson style, it is epic and grand and complex. There's always more to the story than what meets the eye and you follow the characters on the journey, especially Wax, as they're trying to solve it themselves. You are as confused as the characters are. I mean, once you start reading Sanderson's books, you just give up on even trying to guess what the plot twits are, because he's leagues ahead. And Sanderson is a genius, so that doesn't help either. <br /><br />And I can't forget to mention his classic avalanche endings that come barging at you out of nowhere. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There was that slight scare when it was bluntly written on the page that Wax had died. I mean, what the fuck?! I would've been so angry! Sanderson just can't pull another Kelsier on us, he needs to ban that trope from his stories! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The world-building, again, is just epic. Phenomenal. It expands a ton-load on the original Mistborn trilogy and this will sound like a broken record since every reviewer that is familiar with his work would have mentioned it, but HOW DOES HE DO IT? Where do these ideas pop out from? Does he have a metal mind that stores up all of his ideas? I mean, there's no other explanation for it. That has to be it! It was ingenious as always.<br /><br />It's all very Sherlock Holmes style, which was incredible and so enjoyable to read.<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br />Well, this is where the book excelled for me. Marasi, Steris, Melaan and our main boys, Wax and Wayne. They're a duo of the strongest kind. Cannot be separated. The true definition of Yin and Yang. They're dynamic was written insanely well! Wax being the thinker, and Wayne being the light-hearted one in the relationship. Sanderson described him best when he said that <i>Wayne has enough eccentricity for three characters.</i> That man was born to stand out!<br /><br />This is another thing I appreciated and loved about this spin-off. How light-hearted and hilarious it was.<br /><br /><b>“Nice flower,” the kandra said. “Can I have your skeleton when you’re dead?”<br />“My…” Wayne felt at his head.<br />“You’re a Bloodmaker, correct? Can heal yourself? Bloodmaker bones tend to be particularly interesting, as your time spent weak and sickly creates oddities in your joints and bones that can be quite distinctive. I’d love to have your skeleton. If you don’t mind.”<br />Taken aback by this request, Wayne stopped in place. Then he ran past him, pushing into the room where Wax and Steris were talking. “Wax,” he complained, pointing, “the immortal bloke is being creepy again.”</b><br /><br />Isn't he just adorable?! :P<br /><br />I'm going to stop here before I start writing an essay on these characters.<br />Overall, I loved it. Of course I did. It is Brandon Sanderson. He cannot do no wrong in my eyes. The man just knows his shit!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15618864054048703133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2063326565?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378576" href="/book/show/24019186-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2063326565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16808541563365848047">I seriously have no idea why I'm not giving this 5 stars, I love everything about this book, but I still feel like its missing something. This is my favourite in the Alloy era, lots of twists and turns, amazing locations and lots of lovable new characters that I can't wait to read more about them in the final book. I still love the original characters, Wax,Wayne, Marasi, Steris and MeLaan, non of them annoyed me which is a rarity in a series. They made lots of amazing decisions that got them out</span>
  <span id="freeText16808541563365848047" style="display:none">I seriously have no idea why I'm not giving this 5 stars, I love everything about this book, but I still feel like its missing something. This is my favourite in the Alloy era, lots of twists and turns, amazing locations and lots of lovable new characters that I can't wait to read more about them in the final book. I still love the original characters, Wax,Wayne, Marasi, Steris and MeLaan, non of them annoyed me which is a rarity in a series. They made lots of amazing decisions that got them out of really bad situations.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Nice flower,” the kandra said. “Can I have your skeleton when you’re dead?”<br />“My…” Wayne felt at his head.<br />“You’re a Bloodmaker, correct? Can heal yourself?<br />Taken aback by this request, Wayne stopped in place. Then he ran past him, pushing into the room where Wax and Steris were talking. “Wax,” he complained, pointing, “the immortal bloke is being creepy again.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>World building and Writing </u><br />Since I've already discussed this in my review of alloy of law, I won't say much about it here to avoid repitition. There is a lot of improvement in both the world building and writing that I really like. The new locations was perfectly interwoven into the story and the writing just gets better.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Gettin’ old,” Wayne said with a grin, passing him and starting up the next ladder.<br />“Don’t be dense,” Wax said, grabbing the ladder below him and climbing. “I’m trying to pace myself. What if we reach the top and have to fight?”<br />“You can throw your wooden teeth at ’em,” Wayne said from above. “Do some cane waggin’ as well. I’m sure you’re cross about stayin’ up so late.”<br />"I should deck you right in your grin,” he grumbled as he joined the still-smiling Wayne on the catwalk. “But you’d just heal.”<br />“Nah,” Wayne said. “I’d fall over and groan. Considerin’ your age, it’s more important to make you feel you’ve accomplished somethin’ in a day.”<br />“If I shot you,” Wax said, “nobody would blame me. They’d probably just say, ‘Wow. You lasted that long? I’d have shot him years ago.’ Then they’d buy me a pint.”<br />“Now, that hurts, it does,” Wayne said.</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>Characters </u><br />This is my favourite thing in this book. The characters are one in a million type. They all have different personalities and are unique in their own way even though they have the same goal. <br /><b>Wax</b> was all action than words as usual, I also love that he is a startegist. Its also nice that he finally forgave himself.<br /><b>Wayne</b> and his crazy sense of morality, it finally paid off here, I love his loyalty to Wax is unquestionable, I hope he forgive himself in the next book for what he did in the past.<br /><b>Marasi</b> is even more badass than before, she still felt like a shadow sometimes but she moved on and didn't let it hold her back, I for one like the decision she made after she made peace with herself.<br /><b>MeLaan</b>, go girl, she is even more badass than TenSoon, I love how blunt she is about what she is.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Gonna be hard to sneak in there,” Wayne said.<br />“You could kill one of the guards for me,” MeLaan said, settling onto a rock. “I’d eat him, take his shape, and slip us in that way.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Steris</b>,really surprised me here, I realize that I wrongly misjudged her, she is weird and all but she is more flexible than people give het credit for, and she is not cold at all just reserved.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>He glanced at her, then down at her purse. “They searched your purse.”<br />“That they did,” she said, then took the hem of her skirt, lifting it up to the side and revealing a small handgun strapped to her thigh. “I worried they’d do something like that. So I made other plans.”<br />Wax grinned. “I could get used to having you around, Steris.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I sure love the way things ended for her.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She fell in love with Wax and he returned her feelings, even made their wedding romantic, its no longer marriage about political allies and connection but love. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_1763338724" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1763338724" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1763338724?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765387790" href="/book/show/28812157-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763338724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11242797874109371180"><b>4.5/5 stars</b><br/><br/>Out of all the 3 books available so far in Wax & Wayne stories, this is definitely the best one. While reading the last 30% of this book, I seriously wondered how the hell does Sanderson keeps on coming with all these new ideas? I mean seriously, genius is an understatement at this point.<br/>In Bands of Mourning, he showed the potential future for Mistborn franchise and believe me, it will be huge and after reading this one, I'm full with confidence all of them will maintain their great q</span>
  <span id="freeText11242797874109371180" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 stars</b><br /><br />Out of all the 3 books available so far in Wax &amp; Wayne stories, this is definitely the best one. While reading the last 30% of this book, I seriously wondered how the hell does Sanderson keeps on coming with all these new ideas? I mean seriously, genius is an understatement at this point.<br />In Bands of Mourning, he showed the potential future for Mistborn franchise and believe me, it will be huge and after reading this one, I'm full with confidence all of them will maintain their great quality. <br /><br />I'm going to divide this review into 3 main point. Plot, actions and then characters.<br /><br />Plot: <br />Firstly, it's almost impossible to write a comprehensive review on this point without mentioning some of the major spoiler so I'll just make this really brief and spoiler-free. The plot in this book, especially the last 30% the book is equivalent to the level of original Mistborn trilogy imo. Some major twist and revelations happened throughout the book, the ending was beautiful, and most of all the epilogue will show you clearly just what Sanderson planned for this franchise. Literally down to the last word of the book. The plot by itself will keep you entertained and left you wanting for more.<br /><br />Actions: <br />The book this time are filled with lot of actions compared to previous Shadows of Self and believe me, the actions is damn good for reason again I cannot mention. Click at your own risk <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Marasi &amp; Wax holding the power of a Mistborn! how epic was that!? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> You won't be disappointed by the amount and quality of the actions in this book and if you know Sanderson's work by now, you know he is the master of creating a great climax on the last 20-30% in any of the book he wrote. Whether it's plot-driven, action-driven, or both (90% of the time ended up in both) you'll know he always conclude his book with a bang or something to look forward to.<br /><br />Characters:<br />While I say this part will be about the characters development in the book, let me clarify this will consist 90% of me talking about only one person. For those of you who've read this book, you know who I'm talking about. Steris!!! It's just crazy just how much an improvement Sanderson wrote towards this character, she is now my favorite character of the Wax &amp; Wayne series, along with Wayne, well cause you know, it's Wayne. Steris doesn't shine any at all in her brief appearance in Alloy of Law so I was pretty neutral about her, then she appeared again a bit longer with several improvements and her funny social awkwardness in Shadows of Self which make me kinda like her. Finally, in this book boom, we know about her a LOT and oh boy, she is such a lovable character. Read this book now and be prepare to love another fictional character! I know you have tons of them already, why not add 1 more and a pretty interesting one at that? She is neat, funny, always have backup plans, sweet &amp; realistic. While Wayne are there to made you laugh, Steris are definitely in the book to warm your heart. If you don't feel warm at all about the relationship between Wax &amp; Steris, even after knowing Wax's history and what Steris meant to him now, seriously pour yourself a cup of water with 100 degree celcius boiling degree and splash that damn cup to your chest to warm your frozen heart. The ending <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[where Wax finally married Steris out of love, not obligation <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is just beautiful and I admit, I smiled (with a little bit of glassy eyes) out of pure happiness.<br /><br />Well there's my review on The Bands of Mourning. Sanderson mentioned that Mistborn, along with Stormlight Archive is two of his franchise that he will be working on til the end of his career and we still have at least 7 more books in the Mistborn franchise. "The Lost Metal" which is the last part of Wax &amp; Wayne's adventure, a new trilogy set in contemporary setting and finally, the last trilogy set in futuristic sci-fi setting. I can safely say, I'll be joining all his adventures in the franchise and be damn glad to do so. Now, I'll be joining the waiting game with fellow fans and friends on the Lost Metal which most probably will release in 2018. 0_0'<br /><br />Note: Sanderson mentioned it's better to start Secret History only after finishing Bands of Mourning so yeah, you should follow his advice :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11242797874109371180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2936737748" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2936737748?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473208278" href="/book/show/26541448-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ✨ A ✨  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/58818027-fares">Fares</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=cross-post">cross-post</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy">faves-adult-scifi-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=all-the-stars-in-the-sky">all-the-stars-in-the-sky</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2936737748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12216135500380587196">Seriously people, if you're on the hedge about whether to start this series or not — GET 👏 TO👏 IT 👏. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>“I’ve been a lot of people, Ladrian. Seen through a lot of eyes. There’s always another perspective, if you look hard enough.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>What are the Bands of Mourning? Rumoured to be metal minds of legend, said to grant the beholder incredible power. Most people don't believe <i>The Bands</i> made it through the <i>Catacendre</i> and that their existence is only a myth. <br/><br/>Wax was of the same thought until a Kandra res</span>
  <span id="freeText12216135500380587196" style="display:none">Seriously people, if you're on the hedge about whether to start this series or not — GET 👏 TO👏 IT 👏. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I’ve been a lot of people, Ladrian. Seen through a lot of eyes. There’s always another perspective, if you look hard enough.”</b>
</i><br><br>What are the Bands of Mourning? Rumoured to be metal minds of legend, said to grant the beholder incredible power. Most people don't believe <i>The Bands</i> made it through the <i>Catacendre</i> and that their existence is only a myth. <br><br>Wax was of the same thought until a Kandra researcher returns from the south, injured, with evidence of their existence. But the Kandra was not the only one in search of <i>The Bands</i>. <br><br>Wax, Wayne, Marasi, Steris and MeLaan are sent to investigate and try to stop <i>The Bands of Mourning</i> from falling into the wrong hands. <br><br><br>Whenever I finish one of Sanderson's books I'm filled with a <i>hunger</i> for more. Knowing that there are plenty more of his books for me to make my way through, as well as all the new content he has planned, fills me with such immense joy. The future of this franchise is a bright one.<br><br>The writing style, fast pace, action and ‘quest’ nature of this book kept me hooked. I usually read multiple books at the same time but I found I could not concentrate on anything else. When I wasn't reading, I was thinking about this book and it's characters — wondering how Sanderson in next going to blow me away!<br><br>The plot took a different turn, that I was not expecting. Sanderson melded magic <i>with</i> technology in a way that was so fantastic. I have no idea how he comes up with these ideas but they are nothing short of incredible. <br><br>The crew basically go on an adventure outside of Elendel this time and it was so fun reading about. Their interactions, banter and growth in their relationships were, as always, a joy. I cannot get enough of them. <br><br>Wax as always is so entertaining to read about. I know he fills the stereotypical hero trope but I still love him anyway. At the beginning of this book he is still raw and hurt from the things he had to endure and it was beautiful to see him slowly heal those wounds. <br><br>Steris's growth as a character and how beloved she became to me is <i>astounding</i>. I did not really have any feelings towards her in Alloy of Law, since she was only in a few scenes. But then in Shadows of Self I came to really like her. We share a couple of similarities like my obsessiveness with lists and having the tendency to carry a thousand things in my bag <i>‘just in case’</i> 😂. Her social awkwardness was also so comforting and relateble. And I loved the way both she and Wax are able to bond about not fitting in. <br><br>Wax and Steris's interactions were of my favourite parts. It warmed my heart to see them find solace in one another. And I'm definitely on that ship. <br><br><blockquote>“Steris, I think we’re all like that. Shuffled from place to place by duty, or society, or God Himself. It seems like we’re just along for the ride, even in our own lives. But once in a while, we do face a choice. A real one. We may not be able to choose what happens to us, or where we’ll stop, but we point ourselves in a direction.”</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1583152129ra/29046109.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wayne is the ray of sunshine in this series. Although he exasperates everyone, they still cherish him because you can't help but love this guy! I hope we get more about him in the next book because I think there is still unexplored depths to his character that we need. <br><br>Marasi's growth and self reflection was also really good. She's discovered who she is and what kind of impact she would like to make. And I'm really happy with the direction her character growth has taken. <br><br>The plot twists and grand reveals were as expected — executed brilliantly. There were some things I predicted <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like Wax's two faced sister <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and things that took me so much by surprise that I found myself exclaiming out loud <i>‘WHAT!’</i> many times. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479170241ra/21155856.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am filled with questions and I have pages of notes. I cannot wait for the Last Metal, which I'm really hoping will be coming to us soon! <br><br>[after this I'm reading The Secret History (Mistborn #3.5) which Sanderson suggests is to be read after BOM] <br><br><i>
  <b>“I’ve been a lot of people, Ladrian. Seen through a lot of eyes. There’s always another perspective, if you look hard enough.”</b>
</i><br>___<br><b>My reviews for:</b><br><br><i>Era One</i><br><br>0.5 (short story): <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2608045644" rel="nofollow noopener">The Eleventh Metal</a><br>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2604499760" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606309355" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Ascension</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2605049392" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero of Ages</a><br><br>Book 3.5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737859" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a><br><br><br><i>Era Two</i><br>Book 4: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936736710" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a><br>Book 5: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2936737014" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadows of Self</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1915579765" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1915579765" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1915579765?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378576" href="/book/show/24019186-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1915579765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9461563802649659204">I’m not sure I can write a review of this book that does it any kind of justice. I try to write reviews that actually contain some kind of cohesive thoughts about the book, but I’m afraid all I can do is gush right now. Bands of Mourning was absolutely fantastic from beginning to end. I enjoyed myself immensely, and am so looking forward to any and all Mistborn stories Sanderson puts out in the future. Or any stories in the Cosmere, honestly. I just really love Sanderson, okay?!<br/><br/>There was so much</span>
  <span id="freeText9461563802649659204" style="display:none">I’m not sure I can write a review of this book that does it any kind of justice. I try to write reviews that actually contain some kind of cohesive thoughts about the book, but I’m afraid all I can do is gush right now. Bands of Mourning was absolutely fantastic from beginning to end. I enjoyed myself immensely, and am so looking forward to any and all Mistborn stories Sanderson puts out in the future. Or any stories in the Cosmere, honestly. I just really love Sanderson, okay?!<br /><br />There was so much character development here, especially from Steris. I know there are those who think that Sanderson fails at crafting believable, sympathetic characters. I’ve read some reviews that go so far as to say that his characters tend to be cardboard. I simply can’t agree. But I will say that his characters have become warmer and more genuine to me in his later books. I’m more attached to Wax and Wayne and the gang than I was to Vin and Elend, though I really enjoyed their story. I never saw a lack in his writing, but he’s done nothing but improve with every book he publishes. And I really love how he brings back characters from other books in different forms and capacities. (Those who have already read this know exactly who I’m talking about. One in particular. I had to give myself literally <i>hours</i> after finishing this book to be able to think of anything but a certain reappearance.<br /><br />Just about everyone can agree that Sanderson excels at world building and magic systems and incredibly engaging action scenes and plot twists. This book and the books that preceded it were no exception. There was never a dull moment. There was humor, devastation, joy, shock, awe, and romance to be found within these pages. As my beautiful friend Mary pointed out, Sanderson gave an amazing gift to his fans with these Alloy Era books. There were new characters and adventures in a fascinating new time period, but in a world his fans had already fallen in love with. He knocked it out of the park, and I can’t wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23947089.The_Lost_Metal__Mistborn___7_" title="The Lost Metal (Mistborn, #7) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Metal</a>. No really, I can’t…<br /><br />For more of reviews, as well as my own fiction and thoughts on life, check out my blog, <a>Celestial Musings</a><br /><br />I finished up this amazing series (or what there is of it so far!) with my darling, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9461563802649659204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1251040647" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1251040647" />
    <a title="Mario" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16628840-mario"><img alt="Mario" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588674821p2/16628840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1251040647?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario" href="/user/show/16628840-mario">Mario</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16628840-mario?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1251040647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16844804770099215371"><i>Survive.</i><br/><br/><br/><i>Firstly I should say that this review will contain some spoilers but I will put that spoiler sign (or whatever it's called) every time I spoil something </i><br/><br/>HOLY SHIT THIS BOOK WAS GOOD!!!! Previous two books were amazing and they blew me away, but this book blew me away on a completely new level. I've said this many times (and I'll probably say it many times in the future) I don't know how Sanderson does it. How is his writing so perfect?! And even when I think that I've gotten used to his </span>
  <span id="freeText16844804770099215371" style="display:none"><i>Survive.</i><br /><br /><br /><i>Firstly I should say that this review will contain some spoilers but I will put that spoiler sign (or whatever it's called) every time I spoil something </i><br /><br />HOLY SHIT THIS BOOK WAS GOOD!!!! Previous two books were amazing and they blew me away, but this book blew me away on a completely new level. I've said this many times (and I'll probably say it many times in the future) I don't know how Sanderson does it. How is his writing so perfect?! And even when I think that I've gotten used to his writing, he writes another book and it blows me away again. He is without a doubt my favorite author.<br /><br />Now about the book... First thing I should mention is the prologue. As usual, the prologue was about Wax's past, and I loved reading about that (especially now that his sister was in it <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who turned out to be a major bitch <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>). Then we came back to present and things got even better. I loved that Sanderson expanded the world in this book so much. Reading about Investiture<br />and Identity was really interesting, and I hope that they will play big part in the last book. <br /><br />Then I wanna mention the character and AMAZING character development (especially Marasi and Steris). I loved chemistry between Wax and Wayne, and I think that their conversations were one of my favorite parts of the book (I also loved the friendship between Marasi and Wayne). Wayne remained to be my favorite character, but surprisingly, Marasi became my second favorite (sorry Wax). She completely blew me away in this book. In one scene she reminded me of Vin so much (that scene also was the most badass scene in whole Wax and Wayne series-Marasi kicked some ASS). One more thing I want to mention is the relationship between Wax and Steris. Sanderson handled their relationship so well, so I definitely ship it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[since i mention shipping, another surprise were Wayne and MeLaan. I never thought I'd say this but I loved the idea of them together! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But then, after I thought all the surprises were over, came the Epilogue. After I first read the last few sentences and I didn't quite understand what happened, so I just shrugged and read it again (few times actually). And then it hit me. And oh boy, my mind was BLOWN. Sanderson YOU CAN'T JUST END A BOOK LIKE THAT!!! Damn I hate cliffhangers. But on the bright side, I can't even imagine just how amazing the last book in this series will be. It has potential to be right there with <i>Hero of Ages</i> (which is my favorite book ever). I just don't know how I'll survive until it comes out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16844804770099215371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1135280238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135280238" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135280238?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378576" href="/book/show/24019186-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=brandon-sanderson">brandon-sanderson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135280238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1411662315138357792">Ladies and gentlemen, let me present to you, a master of sequels, action scenes and "the last 20%". Mr Sanderson, please take a bow!<br/><br/>Talk about taking it to the next level! The only sequel of Sanderson's which fell short for me was The Well of Ascension; this one however suffers no such disinclination. Bands of Mourning relived some of the epicness of the initial trilogy while still maintaining the tone of a detective story coupled with a grand adventure more suited to this era. And in the vein o</span>
  <span id="freeText1411662315138357792" style="display:none">Ladies and gentlemen, let me present to you, a master of sequels, action scenes and "the last 20%". Mr Sanderson, please take a bow!<br /><br />Talk about taking it to the next level! The only sequel of Sanderson's which fell short for me was The Well of Ascension; this one however suffers no such disinclination. Bands of Mourning relived some of the epicness of the initial trilogy while still maintaining the tone of a detective story coupled with a grand adventure more suited to this era. And in the vein of this era's Mistborn books thus far, this is a fast-paced story with some really cool action scenes. <br /><br />One of the questions I've always had in my mind when Sanderson said that the Mistborn series will span multiple eras was how he will incorporate the magic system into technological advances - Bands of Mourning definitely provided some insight here. Keeping true to his own laws, Sanderson expands on the metallurgic magic system of Scadrial by going deeper into the concepts and introducing cool, new and modern ways of applying Allomancy, Feruchemy and Hemalurgy. <br /><br />Epicness and cool magic system aside, a book is nothing without its characters. Wax is.. well.. Wax - a force of nature, born of two worlds, and in my mind, kind of hot. His interactions with Wayne are always entertaining and the reader can sense the depth and strength of the friendship/partnership between these two characters. I particularly loved this exchange:<br /><br /><i>"Focus, Wayne," Wax said. "How are we going to get in? Shall we try Fat Belt?"<br />"Nah," Wayne said, "too loud. I think we should do Spoiled Tomato."<br />"Dangerous," Wax said, shaking his head. "I'd have to do the placement just right.."<br />"You can do it. You make shots like that all the time.. "<br />"A mistake could ruin the whole infiltration, healing power or no," Wax said. "I think we should do Duck Under Clouds instead."<br />"You kiddin'?" Wayne said. "Didn't you get shot last time we tried that?"<br />"Kinda," Wax admitted.<br />"Tube Run," Wayne said<br />"No glue."<br />"Banefielder?"<br />"Too dark"<br />"Blackwatch Doublestomp"<br />Wax hesitated. "... The hell is that?"<br />"Just made it up," Wayne said, grinning. "It's a nifty code name though, eh?"</i><br /><br />No one doubts that Wayne will yet again deliver his unusual yet humorous spin of logic. MeLaan was also equally hilarious and extraordinary (that's really kind of her nature). Marasi has her moments, which was an improvement from the last book, but with such a stellar cast of characters, she was kind of left in the shadows most of the times.<br /><br />The new star of this series to me was Steris-who has truly come into her own. Her character development was fantastic and I absolutely adore her!! It's really been a very long while since I was this taken by a female character and I applaud Sanderson for nailing it this time-a woman who is <i>"so full of logic and yet so full of wonder at the same time"</i>. <br /><br />The scope in Bands of Mourning extends way beyond the confines of Elendel and without giving away too much, we get quite a decent amount of worldbuilding, as well as hints of something bigger and badder to come. The last 20%, not surprisingly, was a roller-coaster of twists and turns. Even then, Sanderson was not done until the very last paragraph and last word of the book. Diabolical genius!<br /><br />On this note, to gain the maximum experience from this series, please read Mistborn : Secret History AFTER Bands of Mourning. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1411662315138357792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
