<div id="review_1396797116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1396797116" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1396797116?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=arcs-and-galleys">arcs-and-galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1396797116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18075769972728846401">4 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/01/25/book-review-the-bands-of-mourning-by-brandon-sanderson/'>http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/01/25/b...</a><br/><br/>2016 is another big year for Brandon Sanderson with a whole slew of new book releases and re-issues coming out, and he’s kicking it all off in late January with The Bands of Mourning. This is the sixth Mistborn novel and third volume of Waxillium Ladrian’s saga following on the heels of Shadows of Self, and according to Sanderson one is an intentional counterpoint to the other, which explains why there were only a few mont</span>
  <span id="freeText18075769972728846401" style="display:none">4 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/01/25/book-review-the-bands-of-mourning-by-brandon-sanderson/">http://bibliosanctum.com/2016/01/25/b...</a><br /><br />2016 is another big year for Brandon Sanderson with a whole slew of new book releases and re-issues coming out, and he’s kicking it all off in late January with The Bands of Mourning. This is the sixth Mistborn novel and third volume of Waxillium Ladrian’s saga following on the heels of Shadows of Self, and according to Sanderson one is an intentional counterpoint to the other, which explains why there were only a few months to wait between the books. For readers like myself, that decision to publish them so close together was much appreciated, since I don’t think I could have waited until the end of the year to find out what happens, especially after that shocking ending in Shadows of Self.<br /><br />Things come to a head in The Bands of Mourning, continuing the adventures of Waxillium and his companions. It has been six months since the events of Shadows of Self and our heroes are still recovering from the ordeal. Wax himself is still trying to come to terms with what happened but is also determined to move on with his life, and one of the first orders of business is his forthcoming marriage to Steris. But before the couple can tie the knot, a kandra brings tidings of a possible new discovery in the mountains.<br /><br />Legends say that the Lord Ruler created a pair of metalminds called the Bands of Mourning that are so powerful that anyone who wears them will have all the Allomantic abilities at their command. Most believe that they are a thing of myth, but now a kandra researcher has returned to Elendel with drawings that look suspiciously like the Bands. Unable to resist the call of adventure, Wax agrees to travel south with the kandra MeLaan to investigate, bringing along Steris as well as his friends Marasi and Wayne. However, Wax was wholly unprepared to stumble across news of his lost sister along the way, and the quest for the Bands unexpectedly takes a dangerous turn as it puts him on the trail of Edwarn Ladrian, Wax’s unscrupulous uncle who is also involved with the shadowy organization known as The Set.<br /><br />After so many books in the Mistborn series, I didn’t think I could be surprised anymore, but I was wrong. Most of the story in The Bands of Mourning does not take place in the Roughs nor does it take place in the city of Elendel, instead taking us out into the outskirts of the Basin. We’ve been with Wax for so long, it’s easy to forget there’s a whole wide world out there beyond the frontier regions or the urban areas, and the first stop is beautiful New Seran. Sanderson may be best known for his magic systems, but he is also a master at creating new places and bringing them to life. With its luscious fields of fruit and majestic waterfalls, the awe-inspiring vistas of New Seran make me think this could be Sanderson’s version of Rivendell or Naboo. Next up are the cold icy mountain ranges bordering the Basin, where the final chapters of the book take place. There’s also a farther, more mysterious place that I can’t really speak of for fear of spoilers, but regardless, out of all the novels in this series I think it’s safe to say this one expands the world the most, at least geographically.<br /><br />The story does not disappoint either. It’s an action-filled romp through a fantasy world on the cusp of an industrial revolution, and the Western vibes are still strong with this book, which even includes scenes from a spectacular train robbery. Also, despite The Bands of Mourning taking place half a year after Shadows of Self and featuring a whole new adventure, the two books do indeed tie together when you look at it from the perspective of Wax’s personal growth. It is an emotional journey that brings resolution to the many questions our protagonist has been struggling with since the last book, and it also marks an end to one chapter while opening another. New possibilities are on the horizon, including the potential for new worlds, new relationships, and perhaps even a new villain. You might be able to get away with reading this on its own, but I do highly recommend picking up Shadows of Self first, or better yet, start Wax’s story from the beginning with The Alloy of Law (which is still my favorite of the new Wax and Wayne Mistborn novels).<br /><br />Another thing I loved about this book? The supporting characters! The story is once again carried by POVs from our three usual suspects—Wax, Wayne and Marasi—but my favorite characters in this book were actually Steris and MeLaan. As usual, there was plenty of humor especially in the dialogue, and the best of that came in the form of interactions between Wayne and MeLaan, a brilliant pairing. But perhaps the greatest surprise of the novel was Steris. She always struck me as rather austere and aloof in previous books, but we finally get to see a lot more of her true self here. And maybe I’m biased, because I recognize a lot of myself in her uptight planning and obsessive list-making behavior, but out of all the characters, I felt she was the most sympathetic. I’m really excited to see what might be in store for her and Wax, because Sanderson really did a great job developing their relationship.<br /><br />Overall, The Bands of Mourning is another fantastic installment in the Mistborn sequence. Brandon Sanderson fans will be sure to love this one, especially if you’ve been following the books and keeping up with Wax and the gang. You definitely won’t want to miss this rusting good read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18075769972728846401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I know some of you has experienced this so I’m sorry in advance because this review would be an incoherent rambling of a lunatic.<br/><br/>330 years after that “shit that went down” on the Hero of Ages, Scadrial ( formerly known as the Land of Abundant Ashes) is now teeming with electricity and technology. Technically, just imagine the love child of Victorian Era and Wild Wild West wi</span>
  <span id="freeText6328972397713931653" style="display:none"><br><b>Spoiler free review because I'm not entirely heartless.</b><br><br>You know how hard it is to write a review for a book that you love. I know some of you has experienced this so I’m sorry in advance because this review would be an incoherent rambling of a lunatic.<br><br>330 years after that “shit that went down” on the Hero of Ages, Scadrial ( formerly known as the Land of Abundant Ashes) is now teeming with electricity and technology. Technically, just imagine the love child of Victorian Era and Wild Wild West with Allomancy (you get the idea). In this world,we have <b>Waxillium “Wax” Ladrian (Lord of the Ladrian House and is a lawman), Wayne (who is just pure awesome and is Wax’s BFF) and Marasi (she’s okay.)</b><br><br>This is the third book in the Wax and Wayne’s Adventure in Scadrial (no,this is not the official title) and sooo many things have happened that I can’t talk about unless you’ve already read the books.<br><br>I love this series.I know that a lot of people are disappointed that it’s different than the first trilogy but I think it’s good that it was written that way. If “The Wax and Wayne’s Adventure in Scadrial Trilogy” became exactly like “The Trilogy of So Much Feels” then I would have just compared them and be bitter about it because the 2 trilogies were helluva awesome the same way that pizza and pecan pie are both good but in an entirely different way.<br><br>After reading this book, I have to suppress my fangirling because my friends aren’t finished with the book yet. <i>*sideway glare at friends because they're not finished yet*</i><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454530229ra/17977586.gif" width="245" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Bromance between Wax and Wayne is one of the best things that Sanderson gave in this book.How many male MCs do you know that has an amazing platonic relationship with each other? Wax and Wayne’s bromance were the best.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Sure, sure,”Wayne said.”It’s okay,mate. Most folks put on a little weight as they hit their twilight years.’S natural and all.”<br><br>“If I shot you,” Wax said,”nobody would blame me.They’d probably just say, “Wow. You lasted that long?I’d have shot him years ago.’ Then they’d buy me a pint.”</i>
</b><br><br>Of course, the characters really grow in this book. One example is Steris. Yes, I didn’t like her in the first book.I was #teamMarasi at first. Then book two came and she has this wonderful moment with Wax that made me change sides immediately. Then in this book, everyone is gushing about her because SHE’S SO BADASS SHE ROCKS!!<br><br>I’m not sure about you guys, but I’m shipping these two.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452246023ra/17665564.gif" width="245" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454530229ra/17977587.gif" width="324" height="183" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454530229ra/17977588.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then, how I can forget?<b> Wayne has a potential shipmate in this book</b>! *screaming*<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454530229ra/17977589.gif" width="245" height="193" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454530229ra/17977590.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then out of the blue, B.S gave us another shocking revelation.Like “What?What the hell is that?”<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453308676ra/17811082.gif" width="500" height="228" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending killed me. <s>I can’t believe B.S ended the book that way.</s> Oh wait,I can. Now I can’t wait for the next book,damn you Sanderson.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454530229ra/17977591.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1815517572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11580675078579456719">Dammit! Why didn't I have more willpower?! I know a lot of Sanderson fans are waiting for this trilogy to be finished before they would even start. I smugly jumped in , deep in my early gratification, thoroughly enjoying the books. BUT NOW IM SORRY! Because there is soooo long to go for the next one!<br/><br/>This was brilliant and also making me very excited about the third era of trilogies that there will eventually be. I am of course not going to be including spoilers but I will say that I felt very di</span>
  <span id="freeText11580675078579456719" style="display:none">Dammit! Why didn't I have more willpower?! I know a lot of Sanderson fans are waiting for this trilogy to be finished before they would even start. I smugly jumped in , deep in my early gratification, thoroughly enjoying the books. BUT NOW IM SORRY! Because there is soooo long to go for the next one!<br /><br />This was brilliant and also making me very excited about the third era of trilogies that there will eventually be. I am of course not going to be including spoilers but I will say that I felt very differently about Steris by the end of the book and the technology and other new elements were fantastic.<br /><br />Very recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11580675078579456719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1484329606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484329606" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1484329606?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1484329606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8365333352412734014">I began the first trilogy knowing nothing and then being blown away. I started the second trilogy going, "Huh?", but eventually warming to the interesting characters and setting. After all, the magic system still rocked and turning the series into a western wasn't *that* far out of the realms of possibility.<br/><br/>I wasn't blown away by book 4. I thought book 5 was a good deal better, enjoying the dialog between Wax and Wayne more and more and thoroughly enjoying the thread of lost love and evil gods (</span>
  <span id="freeText8365333352412734014" style="display:none">I began the first trilogy knowing nothing and then being blown away. I started the second trilogy going, "Huh?", but eventually warming to the interesting characters and setting. After all, the magic system still rocked and turning the series into a western wasn't *that* far out of the realms of possibility.<br /><br />I wasn't blown away by book 4. I thought book 5 was a good deal better, enjoying the dialog between Wax and Wayne more and more and thoroughly enjoying the thread of lost love and evil gods (and ineffectual good ones, too. Yeah, I'm looking at you, Harmony.) The new world was one I could respect and like, but I never got to the point where I really loved it.<br /><br />And then this book came around, and after what I thought was a tiny rough beginning, I was delighted to see just how much I loved Wayne's sequence. There was a lot of real beauty in the writing, like a dance of pure chicanery, and I delighted in it. And then, of course, we got Wax's marriage to the wonderful Steris, who is every bit of a match for him, smart and oh-so-damn-prepared. Can I tell you how endearing this woman is with her damn lists? Well, yeah, I guess I can. :)<br /><br />What really makes this novel stands out, though, is not the adventure into steampunkland or the straight adventure into finding the Lord Ruler's own metalmind that allows the wearer full access to all 16 metals and ferrochemical attributes, but the fact that it was done well. We got the huge magical sequence that is reminiscent more of the first trilogy than the more modest (and down-to-earth) effects of books 4 and 5. We've got some big things coming, and I that leads me to make one last comment.<br /><br />I've officially moved from a respect and liking for the second series to a deep and profound love. I've finally warmed to it. The characters really stand out in my mind and they're still talking and quipping, and I'm getting a whole bunch of warm and fuzzies. :) <br /><br />I can honestly say it's only getting better, and all my so-so feelings about the last two have evaporated like mist. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8365333352412734014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1416641932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416641932" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416641932?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=epics">epics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416641932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5387527624325545786">What is better than the concluding book of a Mistborn trilogy? Discovering at the end it is really the third book in a quadrilogy!<br/><br/>OK, bad jokes aside, this was another phenomenal addition to the Cosmere pantheon of stories. Not hat anyone should be surprised by this, this is Bandon Sanderson we are talking about here writing in arguably his most popular series. Calling that a home field advantage is like saying the humans had a home field advantage against the martians in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds' title='The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells' rel='nofollow noopener'>The War of the Worlds</a>. </span>
  <span id="freeText5387527624325545786" style="display:none">What is better than the concluding book of a Mistborn trilogy? Discovering at the end it is really the third book in a quadrilogy!<br /><br />OK, bad jokes aside, this was another phenomenal addition to the Cosmere pantheon of stories. Not hat anyone should be surprised by this, this is Bandon Sanderson we are talking about here writing in arguably his most popular series. Calling that a home field advantage is like saying the humans had a home field advantage against the martians in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8909.The_War_of_the_Worlds" title="The War of the Worlds by H.G. Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Worlds</a>. As always Sanderson delivers compelling characters, a fascinating, twisty-turny story, SHOCKING REVELATIONS (™), and just as many (new, amazing, jaw dropping, life changing) questions as answers.<br /><br />I won't bother to rehash the story since that isn't my style and it has been done in many other places much better than I could hope to manage. Instead let me discuss some of the aspects of this book that I thought were truly standout.<br /><br /><b>Religion</b>: Religion is a funny thing in fantasy books. Often when talking about God or gods in this context a theological entity that is omnipotent/omnipresent/omniscient isn't in play. Instead God/gods are often very, very, VERY powerful entities with access to more knowledge and power than any mortal could hope to achieve. Sometimes they have always existed, sometimes they are the offspring of elder gods, sometimes they are mortals who have ascended to godhood. But in nearly all cases they are limited in someway and can make for very interesting literary characters.<br /><br />In Mistborn, the local god Harmony has taken a bit of a special interest in Wax (if you have to ask who Wax is, I suggest you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244905301?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/775184008?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadows of Self</a> first), using him to achieve Harmony's agenda. Harmony, as those that are familiar with the series know, was once mortal but ascended to godhood, giving him (in so far as a god can have a gender) a more personal perspective on the lives of mortals. Not that such a perspective prevents him from using mortals for his own ends. The end of the previous installment has left Wax a bitter, broken man holding Harmony is deep resentment.<blockquote>
  <i>Poor Wax. That had busted him up right good, it had. And Wayne could see why. Still, an apology? Did people that got killed in a flood expect an apology from God? God did as God wished. You simply hoped to not get on His worse side. Kinda like the bouncer at the club with the pretty sister</i>
</blockquote>So when they talk again in this book it is a fascinating exchange between a them, mortal to mortal-turned-god. It explores what the limits of godhood are and how far they should be pushed (should God eliminate all evil? should God prevent all bad things form happening? Where is the line drawn?). It explores the nature of choice and how Wax has treated himself since the events in Shadows of Self. Harmony shows himself to be an understanding god who offers Wax the choice (as he does with all of humanity) choice in how they live their lives. It illuminating and does an excellent job distilling some serious theological questions into an easily understood and applicable context for the reader.<br /><br />But on a more personal level their conversation really brings out some of Wax's deeply held troubles with a deep compassion and understanding. Harmony, while maintaining what he did was necessary, if painful, allows Wax to work through all his hurt and pain and come to a revelation naturally that allows the healing process to begin. It is a deeply moving passage and touches upon what many of us hope for from such an entity: understanding, wisdom, compassion, and guidance while allowing us mortals the autonomy of choice and self discovery. It is beautifully written and a wonderful advancement in Wax's character not to mention a great peak into the mind and motivations of Harmony.<br /><br /><b>Steris</b>: One of Sanderson's strong suits as a writer is the evolution of characters of the course of his books. We can see clearly how they change and grow but at the same time remain true to their core self. In the case of Steris we are initially introduced to her when she is discussing a very detailed and thorough marriage contract with Wax in 'The Alloy of Law'; a contract that specified the frequency of marital relations, the expected number of heirs, etc. She showed herself to be a very thorough and rational person though she apparently rubbed a fair amount of of my GR friends the wrong way.<br /><br />The core of Steris has always been to be prepared and account for all contingencies. Sure, initially she was a bit of a wet blanket but she really started to find a good groove in 'Shadows of Self' and fully blossomed into awesomeness in 'Bands of Mourning':<i>
  <blockquote>"I need metal," he [Wax] explained at Marasi's inquisitive look.<br /><br />He stepped up to his room, then hesitated as a hand stuck out of the next room, holding a small vial.<br /><br />"Steris?" he said, walking to her. she was still sitting on the plush train bench - though her face was paler than before. "Steel flakes in suspension," she said, wiggling the vial.<br /><br />"Since when have you carried one of these?" Wax asked, taking it from her.<br /><br />"ince about six months ago. I put one into my purse in case you might need it." She raised her other hand, displaying two more. "I carry the other two because I am neurotic."<br /><br />He grinned, taking all thee. He downed the first one, then nearly choked. "What the hell is in this?"<br /><br />"Other than steel?" Steris asked. "Cod-liver oil."<br /><br />He looked at her, gaping.<br /><br />"Whiskey is bad for you, Lord Waxillium. A wife <b>must</b> look out for her husband's health."<br /><br />~~~<br /><br />"Please ignore him," Steris said, rising and walking over. "Here, I've prepared for you a list of possible scenarios that might transpire during our residence here."<br /><br />"Steris..." Wax said, forcing open the thirds and final window.<br /><br />"What?" she demanded. "I will not have the staff unprepared. their safety is our concern."<br /><br />"Fire?" Aunt Gin asked, rading the list. "Shoot-outs. Robbery. Hostage situations. <b>Explosions?</b><br /><br />"That one is completely unfair," Wax said. "You've been listening to Wayne."<br /><br />"Things <b>do</b> explode around you, mate," Wayne said, munching peanuts. Nice bit of salt on these.<br /><br />"He's right, unfortunately," Steris said. "I've accounted for seventeen explosions involving you. That's a huge statistical anomaly, even considering your profession."<br /><br />"You're kidding. Seventeen?"<br /><br />"Afraid so."<br /><br />"Huh." <br /><br />~~~<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["Unexpected," Steris said. And here she assumed she'd been prepared for anything. Marasi starting to glow, throwing people around with Allomancy as if they were dolls, then streaking away and leaving a trail of mist... well that hadn't been on the list. It hadn't even made the <b>appendix</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></blockquote>
</i>Not only is she always trying to take into account and preparing for bad outcomes, but she shows a remarkable amount of courage, loyalty, and cunning in this book. She knows she isn't the most useful person in a fight but she plays to her own strengths as the situation warrants. By the end of this book she was confident in herself and her abilities and is just all around awesome. <br /><br />Now this isn't to say this book was 'The Steris Show' (though I would read the hell out of that book). All the other characters had their moments to shine, especially Marasi who has been dealing with her identity in the shadow (rightly or wrongly) of Wax. The journey our heroes find themselves on forces them to grow and adapt in very fulfilling ways <br /><br /><b>Cosmere/Big Picture</b>: Not to delve too deeply into plot developments, but in this book we are beginning to see the Cosmere books start to get more closely linked together. Apart from the obligatory Hoid appearance we are shown more of the world and how these discoveries will facilitate the binding together of the Cosmere (a hint of which, I believe, was referenced in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1099256161?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Sixth of the Dusk</a>.<br /><br />We also get a further exploration of The Set, their long term goals, how Wax's family fits in, and the organization's mysterious sponsors. We are left with an explosive ending that raises a lot of serious and scary questions. I continue to be in awe of what Sanderson is slowly putting together. The scope and breathe of what the Cosmere will become is simply astounding and I simply cannot wait for each subsequent book in the series.<br /><br />So yes, this book was everything I could have wanted and more. It maintains the high standards of the series and propels it in a new, awesome direction. And man, that epilogue was pretty intense. So waste no time in diving into this one and then you can follow it up with a side of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036-mistborn" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a>.<br /><br />As I often do, here are some of my favorite passages from this book, which was chocked full of some great exchanges:<br /><br /><b>We all have talents, we just don't all love our talents.</b>:<i>"Oi," Wayne said, hustling up beside him. "A good plan that one was, eh?"<br />"It was the same plan you always have," Wax said. "The one where I get to be the decoy."<br />"Ain't my fault people like to shoot at you, mate," Wayne said as they reached the coach. "You should be happy; you're usin' your talents, like me granners always said a man should do."<br />"I'd rather not have 'shootability' be my talent."<br />"Well, you gotta use what you have."</i><br /><br /><b>Religion (and murder) is in the details</b>:<i>You've given up? Is that how the Ascendant Warrior was? Huh?"<br />"No, in fact she walked up to the man she wanted, slapped the book out of his hand, and kissed him."<br />"See, there's how it is!"<br />"Though the Ascendant Warrior also went on and murdered the woman Elend was planning to marry."<br />"What, really?"<br />"Yeah."</i><br /><br /><b>Normal is just a setting on the dishwasher</b>:<i>"They're going after the rest of the train," Wax said, pointing. "The first thieves must have recognized this car as private one, probably lush with riches to plunder, and so they uncoupled it. But something is wrong."<br />"Other than people trying to kill us?" Marasi asked.<br />"No," Steris said, "in my experience, that's quite normal.</i><br /><br /><b>Always check to see what happened to the person you are replacing</b>:<i>"But when Lord Waxillium is around, things <b>do</b> tend to pop up."<br />"Things?" Drewton said. "Pop up? This is a rusting train robbery!"<br />Steris regarded the valet with a cool expression. "Didn't you inquire about your prospective master before entering Lord Waxillium's employ?"<br />"Well, I mean, I <b>knew</b> he had an interest in the constabulary. Like some lords have an interest in the symphony, or in civic matters. It seemed odd, but not ungentlemanly. I mean, it's not as if he was involved in <b>theater</b>...Should we go look?" Drewton asked.<br />"We?"<br />"Well, you." He tugged at his collar." Gunfights. I had not actually expected gunfights. Aren't the servants usually left out of such extravagances?"<br />"Most of the time," Marasi said.<br />"Except when the house blew up," Steris added.<br />"Except then."<br />"And...you know," Steris said.<br />"Best not to mention it."<br />"Mention what?" Drewton asked.<br />"Don't worry about it," Marasi said, glaring at Steris. If the man couldn't do a little research before taking a job -<br />"Wait," Drewton said, frowning. "What exactly happened to Lord Ladrian's <b>previous</b> valet?"</i><br /><br /><br />Not that you really need to get a taste of this book before considering buying it (since if you've gotten to book six in a series you are probably already committed to it) but here are the first six chapters:<br /><br /><a href="http://www.tor.com/2015/12/07/excerpts-brandon-sanderson-the-bands-of-mourning-chapter-one/" rel="nofollow noopener">Chapter 1</a><br /><a href="http://www.tor.com/2015/12/14/the-bands-of-mourning-chapter-two/#more-198923" rel="nofollow noopener">Chapter 2</a><br /><a href="http://www.tor.com/2015/12/21/excerpts-brandon-sanderson-the-bands-of-mourning-chapter-three/" rel="nofollow noopener">Chapter 3</a><br /><a href="http://www.tor.com/2016/01/04/excerpts-brandon-sanderson-the-bands-of-mourning-chapter-four/" rel="nofollow noopener">Chapter 4</a><br /><a href="http://www.tor.com/2016/01/11/excerpts-brandon-sanderson-the-bands-of-mourning-chapter-five/" rel="nofollow noopener">Chapter 5</a><br /><a href="http://www.tor.com/2016/01/18/excerpts-brandon-sanderson-the-bands-of-mourning-chapter-six/" rel="nofollow noopener">Chapter 6</a></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1044485585?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1044485585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10976913443668280821">This third instalment in the second era Mistborn series proved to be the best yet! It was fast paced and stuffed full of action, mystery, humor, romance, cool magic, and shock developments. Sanderson once again succeeded in keeping me fully engaged and entertained for the duration of the story. <br/><br/>All our favourite characters were back. This time on a quest to seek out the bands of mourning, the legendary metalminds of the Lord Ruler, and they are not the only ones hunting the prize as the nefariou</span>
  <span id="freeText10976913443668280821" style="display:none">This third instalment in the second era Mistborn series proved to be the best yet! It was fast paced and stuffed full of action, mystery, humor, romance, cool magic, and shock developments. Sanderson once again succeeded in keeping me fully engaged and entertained for the duration of the story. <br /><br />All our favourite characters were back. This time on a quest to seek out the bands of mourning, the legendary metalminds of the Lord Ruler, and they are not the only ones hunting the prize as the nefarious Set are seeking the bands for themselves. The story was a ton of fun. I loved the mix of action and intrigue and was blown away by some of the shock developments as the story progressed. Sanderson has a real talent for introducing things that totally turn the story on its head! <br /><br />Wax, Wayne, and Marasi were as awesome as they were in the previous books, but the stars of Bands of Mourning were Steris and MeLaan. MeLaan was hilarious in almost every scene she appeared in and is easily my all time favourite Kandra. Steris was fantastic and has really developed as a character since we first met her back in the Alloy of Law. She proved the perfect mix of endearing and hilarious and has fast become one of my favourite Sanderson characters of any of his series! I loved the way pretty much every character showed positive growth in this instalment. <br /><br />I really loved this latest Mistborn book and cannot wait to see what happens in the final book in the series!<br /><br />Rating: 5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: Michael Kramer is always a fantastic narrator, but he might have given a career best performance with this one. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1527704261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527704261" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527704261?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765378576" href="/book/show/24019186-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=fangirl-alert">fangirl-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=teary-eyes">teary-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=favorite-2016-reads">favorite-2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527704261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14997400949454724974">This review will be split into several parts, organized by spoiler level. <i>If you do not meet at least a given level of spoilers, do not read that section.</i> I'm really very serious about this. <br/><br/><b>For the Sanderson-uninitiated:</b><br/>If you read fantasy, or talk to people about fantasy, or have followed me for a while, you've heard of this guy. <i>Bands of Mourning</i> does all the things Sanderson is famous for: it has fast-paced action, carefully applied rules of magic, expansive worldbuilding, and engaging chara</span>
  <span id="freeText14997400949454724974" style="display:none">This review will be split into several parts, organized by spoiler level. <i>If you do not meet at least a given level of spoilers, do not read that section.</i> I'm really very serious about this. <br /><br /><b>For the Sanderson-uninitiated:</b><br />If you read fantasy, or talk to people about fantasy, or have followed me for a while, you've heard of this guy. <i>Bands of Mourning</i> does all the things Sanderson is famous for: it has fast-paced action, carefully applied rules of magic, expansive worldbuilding, and engaging characters. It also, as his latest work, shows clear improvement on many fronts from earlier books: there are more female characters, both in the cast and filling a variety of background roles; the society is clearly multi-ethnic and -racial; and the almost overwhelming ending style known as a 'Sanderlanche' has been significantly smoothed out. (The end is still nigh-impossible to put down, but it's spread out over a longer section of the book, and with a more gradual transition between the rest of the book and the climax.) Also, the main romance is the cutest dang thing.<br /><br />For obvious reasons, this is not a book you can start with. It is at bare minimum the sixth book set on the world of Scadrial, and there are benefits to having read other books in the Cosmere as well. However, if you do pick up one of Sanderson's earlier books and find it weak in some areas - as with the very legitimate criticism of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68428.The_Final_Empire__Mistborn___1_" title="The Final Empire (Mistborn, #1) by Brandon Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire</a> having only one major female character - know that those flaws are corrected over time, and that each book is better than the last.<br /><br /><b>If you've read all of the original Mistborn Trilogy but haven't made the jump:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I know, I know, it's jarring to move forward 300 years, but trust me, it's worth it. Not only do we get to see Scadrial rebuilt and rejuvenated, but there are new uses for the Metallic Arts which were impossible in the era of the Final Empire. The original trilogy had a much tighter focus than this series, focused on the overthrow of the Lord Ruler and the aftermath of that conflict. Here, we see a whole society growing and struggling to determine itself, even as outside influences begin to pose a threat. Some original characters are still around - Sazed, of course - and the rest are remembered in interesting, if not always accurate, ways.<br /><br />Wax, Wayne, Marasi, and Steris are a compelling new cast, with a new dynamic, but the same sort of wisecracking and competence that Kelsier's crew had. And even if Alloy of Law isn't your cup of tea, I suggest you read it anyway, because Shadows of Self and The Bands of Mourning both explore different scales of conflict, and it's almost guaranteed that you'll find something here that catches you the way the first books did. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>If you're caught up to Shadows of Self, but haven't read this one:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This is a very, very different book. SoS was essentially focused on Wax's personal internal conflict, with hints of broader implications; while Bands of Mourning does address his continuing grief/recovery process (and does it beautifully), the focus is mostly on much, much bigger things. Where the first two books stayed focused on the city of Elendel, Bands of Mourning shows the wider Basin and some of the conflicts in it, which Elendel ignores. Everything is tied together: Wax's uncle, his sister's abduction, the resistance of the outer cities to Elendel's control, and the continuing push forward of technology. (Well, almost everything: if you're waiting for an explanation of Trell, keep waiting.)<br /><br />Somewhat unfortunately, as we'll be waiting a while longer for <i>The Lost Metal</i>, this book leaves off at a point of greatest change for the characters and world. I don't think Scadrial's been this shaken up since the Catacendre, and whatever comes next will be fascinating. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>If you're all caught up, but still figuring out this Cosmere thing:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm sure not everyone's on the Wax/Steris train even now, but I sure am. Bonding over studying accounts ledgers? Kissing in midair over the mists? Steris finally getting the honeymoon she wanted? It was pretty much perfect. I also love the way they build each other up, as any good couple should - Steris supporting Wax through his grief, being ready to help with whatever's next; Wax trying his best to contradict her self-deprecation and show her that he thinks she's valuable and worthwhile. <br /><blockquote>Steris started sniffling. She pulled her hand free of his and wiped her eyes.<br />"Is that... good crying or bad?" Wax asked. All these years dealing with women, and he still couldn't tell the difference sometimes.<br />"Well, this wasn't on any of my lists, you see."</blockquote><br />(sounds of me sobbing in the background.)<br />I can't wait for them to be happily married forever. <br /><br />Marasi was a <i>champ</i> in this book, from the very beginning. I love that she told Wayne off for his treatment of Ranette - it's about time someone did that - and seeing the way she's learned to handle a crisis is fascinating. She's still a little unsteady, which is understandable, but she's so <i>courageous</i>. I'm also particularly interested in her relationship with Vin, or rather the mythology of Vin - Marasi at the outset of this series seemed to be a straightforward Action Girl, but in the last two books we've seen her actively questioning that role and whether it's right for her. This is both excellent characterization and an exploration of how history affects societal expectations. Vin was just one woman, but her example has become an ideal, even in the face of Alrianne and Tindwyl's examples. Moreover, Vin's human failings have been erased by time and popular belief:<br /><blockquote>"Were you ever insecure?" Marasi asked. "Or did you always know what to do? Did you get jealous? Frightened? Angry?"<br />If Vin had been an ordinary person at any point, the stories and songs had forgotten.</blockquote><br />The culmination of all of this, of course, is when she takes up the power of the Bands of Mourning. I'll freely admit that I was about in tears in this scene, and that I was kind of disappointed when she gave the power over to Wax (though I saw it coming), but thinking over it I'm okay with this, because:<br /><blockquote>She hovered in the sky, flush with power. In that moment, she <i>was</i> the Ascendant Warrior.</blockquote><br />Marasi has been struggling with a society that demands she follows Vin's example, and holding the Bands would be the culmination of that - of all of these pressures she's been pushing against. In that light, letting it go was definitely the right decision for her. I'm not a fan of how it echoed the end of Well of Ascension - female lead takes up godly power, but gives it up to save the life of a man who then becomes more powerful than her - but since Wax gave up the Bands in turn, I can live with it.<br /><br /><br />Wayne and MeLaan getting together was something I'd kind of seen coming, though I didn't expect it as soon as it happened. They fit, but I'm not as invested in it as I am in Wax and Steris - there just hasn't been enough development. There's potential, but I still wouldn't be surprised if Wayne and Marasi became an item. (I'd be perfectly happy to see Marasi stay solo, or for all three of them to form a triad, but there's some foreshadowing there.)<br /><br />Wayne in general was much better this book than last book. For one thing, he got called out twice - once by Marasi, and once by Wax - for his treatment of Ranette and Steris. He seems to have made a... generally good-faith attempt to apologize to Ranette, crassness aside, and I'm hopeful that for Wax he'll learn to treat Steris with actual kindness. After all, as we saw clearly, his relationship with Wax is his lodestone:<br /><blockquote>"Wax," he said, shaking his head. "No. <i>No.</i> I can't do this without you."<br />"Yes you can. Fight."<br />"Not that part," Wayne said. "The rest of it. Livin'."</blockquote><br />Wayne has PTSD, among other things he's dealing with, and this books' climax gave us a crystal clear view of what Wax means to him: Wax is quite literally Wayne's redemption. Without that - without the one man who believed he was worth saving more than he ever did - Wayne doesn't know how to keep going. That's... really deeply heartbreaking.<br /><br />MeLaan's complete lack of understanding human conversational mores remains hilarious. The entire hotel arrival conversation was hilarious. For a book which threatened civil war and city-destroying weapons, this was a damn funny read.<br /><br />Steris continues to be fantastic, in so many ways. It was confirmed during the Shadows of Self tour that she's on the autism spectrum, and this keeps showing up in little, subtle moments:<br /><blockquote>"Sometimes it amazes me that people like Wayne, or even those kandra, can be so startlingly human when I feel so alien."</blockquote><br />I got into a discussion regarding <i>The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time</i> as a representation of autism recently, and in light of that it's striking to me how well and how sensitively Sanderson builds his ASD characters. They're not caricatures or sensationalizations, but individuals with desires and stumbling blocks like any other characters - and they get to stand in the spotlight like anyone else, too. It's telling to me that the people who have picked up on Sanderson's ASD characters are on the spectrum themselves, and seeing representations of their own experiences in fiction for, sometimes, the first time ever. If you're looking for stereotypes, you won't find them, but if you're looking for people - here they are.<br />Also: Steris getting more accustomed to the bizarre events of Wax's life.<br /><blockquote>The carriage lurched into motion, and Steris leaned out the window, waving farewell to the poor innkeeper.<br />"Framed for murder!" Steris called to her. "It's on page seventeen of the list I gave you! Try not to let them harass our servants too much when they arrive!"</blockquote><br /><br />For the record, I expected Telsin's betrayal - though I thought she was being impersonated by a Kandra and long-since dead. I have a little labelled sticky note over her first appearance to this effect. Half credit for predictions?<br /><br />AND NOW: The southerners. I didn't even guess until I got to the line about 'burned maps' in Chapter 18, but as soon as I read that I <i>knew</i>. Brandon's been teasing this contact for years, but I honestly didn't expect it until the 1980s trilogy, and I certainly didn't expect it to happen in a series which started off as a lighthearted side-project.<br />I am <i>thrilled</i>. Allomantic/feruchemical technology! Societies that are doing exactly what Harmony said the Basin isn't - adapting to the pressure of immediate needs by using what they have in new ways. (Someone on Tumblr recently made a post complaining that they couldn't see new uses for Mistborn's magic system and found it boring for that reason - I'd love to tell that person about this book's revelations.)<br />I'm also super excited about their social system. The way Allik treats Wax (while awkward to read) speaks to the rarity of Allomancers/Feruchemists in their culture. (It's still unclear to me how that happened. We know Kelsier was involved in saving their society after the Catacendre, but that doesn't answer two big questions - one, why didn't Harmony help them; and two, how did the Metallic Arts get to their population in the first place?) As I mentioned in my pre-review, that social system is going to be completely upended by the trade deal Wax and Steris struck at the end of this book. All of a sudden they'll have access to a relative wealth of magic, provided by people who won't (all) demand obeisance the way their native Metalborn seem to. They're going to have to question a fundamental element of their hierarchy, and I can't imagine the southern Metalborn will be too happy about that.<br /><br />By the time this series is done, we're going to see a completely different Scadrial. I still wouldn't rule out civil war in the Basin, particularly as the Set seems invested in creating strife. (Does it strike anyone else as strange that Edwarn Ladrian, advocate of predatory loans on impoverished workers, was advocating against Elendel and in favor of the outer cities?) And of course, there's the threat of weapons which... seem like nothing less than magical nukes.<br /><br />I'd say I hope it doesn't come to that, but this is Sanderson. The safe bet is that it will. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>For the Cosmere-literate and the unspoilable:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HMMMM GODDAMN DID WE LEARN SOME STUFF HERE.<br /><br />Some of it was little and subtle - this isn't really spoilers, but the word for the gold symbol is 'mah', which I thought was neat; I'm not sure if it's the word for gold or the letter name, but either way, cool. The confusion in the account books told us that the numerals for 3 and 4 are visually similar, in a way they aren't in our Roman script, which was a neat detail.<br /><br />Worldhoppers! Hoid was obvious - he's generally not subtle, though I'm surprised Wax didn't recognize him as his former coachman from Shadows of Self. More interesting to me was the woman who was asking Wax about his abilities during the party. Minor spoilers for Secret History but: it's Khriss! At long last, we meet the person the Ars Arcanums are written for! And she's a black female scholar of Investiture! Apparently she figures prominently in the upcoming <i>White Sand</i> graphic novel, and I'm really excited for that. Sanderson also used this scene to deal with a question which I imagine he's gotten a lot of versions of from fans - what does storing weight actually do? (Actually, I think I might have asked a variation of this myself at one point.) I'm not very good at physics, but if I understand her questions and answer well enough, we just learned that storing weight is actually reducing <i>mass</i> in some way. (It's entirely possible I've got this backwards, but the scene seems to point to physics rather than magic, and that <i>is</i> the physics explanation... I think.)<br /><br />We finally know what Connection is good for, and it works <i>exactly</i> like Selish magic systems. Previously I'd assumed the place-dependence of Sel's magic was due to Dominion's influence on the planet, but I was wrong: it's much more related to the Cognitive Realm, apparently. This hints a bit at how worldhoppers can move from planet to planet and still communicate with the local poppulation, though I'm sure they're all using different methods to access it. It may also suggest that some properties of Investiture are innate across all systems - Connection would be one, Lightweaving maybe another (we've seen it on both Roshar and Nalthis), and there's a potential third mentioned in Secret History. More on that when I get to my review of that novella.<br /><br />And last but far from least: Trell.<br /><blockquote>"But you need us!" Suit said. "To rule, to manage civilization on-"<br />"No longer. Recent advances have made civilization here too dangerous. Allowing it to continue risks further advances we cannot control, and so we have decided to remove life on this sphere instead. Thank you for your service; it has been accepted. You will be allowed to serve in another Realm."</blockquote><br />Fan theories about Trell, to my knowledge, have mostly been focused on Paalm's unknown metal spike from Shadows of Self. Personally I'd advocated for it being Endowment, but that got jossed; the prevailing theory was then that it was Autonomy's godmetal. However, after reading this, I don't think Autonomy could be Trell. Aside from the fact that we know Autonomy's Shardholder's name (Bavadin), this statement focuses on <i>control</i> and service to a larger goal, which is the opposite of autonomy. There's a marginal argument to be made that Autonomy preserves its own independence by regulating others, but I'm skeptical of that. Right now, my bet is that Trell is a currently-unknown Shard, since there are nine unaccounted for.<br />HOWEVER. Brandon has been up front about the relevance of color in his works, particularly the significance of red. We've seen it in the Stormlight Archive associated with Odium and the Voidbringers, in "Shadows for Silence in the Forests of Hell" associated with the spirits flying into a killing rage, and in space as Taln's Scar/the Red Rip, which may be the same formation of stars. Given that, we can assume that Trell is either associated with through larger motivation or directly related to these other factors. I doubt it's Odium, but wouldn't rule it out; if it's a Shard whose influence we've seen, though, it seems that Threnody might be the place. Their 'Fallen World' could be another society who became 'too dangerous' for Trell's liking - and the strict control of people's actions by the Simple Rules would be in line with this emphasis on service and regulation.<br /><br />If you'd like to discuss Cosmere speculation in the comments, please put it under a spoiler tag: &lt; spoiler &gt; like so. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="14997400949454724974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2604012711" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2604012711" />
    <a title="Karima chermiti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42944800-karima-chermiti"><img alt="Karima chermiti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521752993p2/42944800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2604012711?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karima chermiti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karima chermiti" href="/user/show/42944800-karima-chermiti">Karima chermiti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25922041-the-bands-of-mourning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=buddy_read">buddy_read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42944800-karima-chermiti?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2604012711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3359344214464953509"><b>
  <i>Mistborn world era 1:</i>
</b><br/><br/>#1: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2366012001?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Final Empire (Mistborn, #1) </a> : 5 stars<br/>#2: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2452491826?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Well of Ascension (Mistborn, #2) </a> : 4.5 stars<br/>#3: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2466603581?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hero of Ages (Mistborn, #3) </a> : 3.5 stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Mistborn world era 2:</i>
</b><br/><br/>#1: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2554396033?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Alloy of Law (Mistborn, #4) </a> : 5 stars<br/>#2: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2564145938?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadows of Self (Mistborn, #5) </a> : 4 stars*<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The difference between good and evil men is not found in the acts they are willing to commit—but merely in what name they are willing to commit them in</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>With each book, I found new ways to love this se</span>
  <span id="freeText3359344214464953509" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Mistborn world era 1:</i>
</b><br><br>#1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2366012001?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Empire (Mistborn, #1) </a> : 5 stars<br>#2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2452491826?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Well of Ascension (Mistborn, #2) </a> : 4.5 stars<br>#3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2466603581?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hero of Ages (Mistborn, #3) </a> : 3.5 stars<br><br><b>
  <i>Mistborn world era 2:</i>
</b><br><br>#1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2554396033?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law (Mistborn, #4) </a> : 5 stars<br>#2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2564145938?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadows of Self (Mistborn, #5) </a> : 4 stars*<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The difference between good and evil men is not found in the acts they are willing to commit—but merely in what name they are willing to commit them in</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>With each book, I found new ways to love this second era more and more. I don’t know how I’m going to manage and wait for the fourth book because that last sentence had me shook. No one writes endings that leave you waiting desperately like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandon Sanderson</a>. It hits you out of nowhere and puts a lot of things into perspective. But let’s backtrack a little before talking about the ending and how mind-blowing it was.<br> <br>In <i>The Bands Of Mourning</i>, the story builds on the events of <i>Shadows Of Self</i> with Wax still dealing with and reeling from what happened in the second book. He is still trying to haunt his uncle down and put an end to the set organization behind all the trouble that he faced since his return to Elendel. But things take a turn to the unexpected when he is recruited by the kandra to find the lord ruler’s Mythical metalminds known as the bands of mournings.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I’m wondering if every person I pass has similar depths, and if there’s any way to avoid the mistake of judging them so shallowly that I’m rocked when they show their true complexity</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I think the major reason why I love this second era so much is that everything I didn’t like about the first era was rectified in this one. What I’m talking about is the female characters and the issues with the story pacing. I already said that I don’t like how three books who are longer than 500 pages each failed to give us more than one important female character who was vital to the plot and the events but in the second era, we meet many female characters who are very vital to the story in different ways, they all have unique personalities, unique characteristics and they all add something different to the books. Marasi, Steris, Melaan and in this book, Wax’s sister. They’re heroes, villains, fighters, thinkers and savers too. They play different roles and they don't fit into one box, they're multi-faceted and well written characters.<br><br>The other things I like is how the characters doesn’t waste time when the situation is crucial and very dangerous, they do their planning and their thinking in a logical amount of time and then they go for it so the books of the second era are fast paced action packed and they have no dull moment even when the characters are just talking or discussing information and revelation, I’m hanging on every word they say because I’m invested in the different arcs and story-lines. I also like how some characters never lose their sense of humor even when they’re facing a certain danger. It brings some levity in an intense book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Plan?” Marasi asked.<br>“Not dyin’.”<br>“Anything more detailed than that?”<br>“Not dyin’ … today?”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I loved how Steris and wax relationship evolved in this book. at first glance, you’d think they’re not that suited to each other but when you see how their relationship grow from an obligation, to fondness to caring deeply about each other to maybe more than that, you release that they are perfect together.<br><br>And Steris is such a breath of fresh air as a female character. She’s levelheaded, she knows her limitations but she also understands the different ways she can be useful. She is no foolish girl and I admire that about her.<br><br>The story had a lot of twists and turns, some I predicted others didn’t see coming but either way I enjoy the way this book kept me on my toes waiting, theorizing and just witnessing all the action and the characters development unfold in the most unexpected ways.<br><br>The ending was phenomenal, I’m not going to say anything about it because spoilers but I can see the fans of this world losing their mind reading that last sentence. Just Don’t toy with me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Brandon Sanderson</a>, I can’t take it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528912186ra/25770639.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>***********************************</b>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>A buddy-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35852954-nadia-awadi" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lovely Nadia</a>
</blockquote><br><br>After the phenomenal and surprising ending of Shadows of Self, I can't wait to discover where the story will take us next, to something great I hope.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3359344214464953509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HrlDuJo+ejwLhHmw8qBRokbX6gFfTOtPjZM/zGWihGDz4qhptk25vFA7CA6FcPUPhOllWlrR/Ogl6gZFJ1sV5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nQgMKtIxxQKSVjmT4uAJArvaoeXzC0mxdAWbJMCvDyZwU+f7/kIGgsnpSC2VMK2veeQuvvaWXhbcfKKtglaeoA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">About Brandon Sanderson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1394044556p3/38550.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38550.Brandon_Sanderson">Brandon Sanderson
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
154,108
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6258173899279839063">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent' title='The Dark Talent' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded' title='Arcanum Unbounded' rel='nofollow noopener'>Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br/>Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul' title='The Emperor’s Soul' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Emperor’s S</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText6258173899279839063" style="display:none">Brandon’s major books for the second half of 2016 are <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18714787.The_Dark_Talent" title="The Dark Talent" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Talent</a>,</i> the final volume in Alcatraz Smedry’s autobiographical account of his battle against the Evil Librarians who secretly rule our world, and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28595941.Arcanum_Unbounded" title="Arcanum Unbounded" rel="nofollow noopener">Arcanum Unbounded</a>,</i> the collection of short fiction in the Cosmere universe that includes the Mistborn series and the Stormlight <br />Archive, among others. This collection features <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28698036.Mistborn__Secret_History" title="Mistborn: Secret History" rel="nofollow noopener">Mistborn: Secret History</a>,</i> and a brand-new Stormlight Archive novella, <i>Edgedancer</i>.<br /><br />Earlier this year he released <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704486.Calamity" title="Calamity" rel="nofollow noopener">Calamity</a>,</i> the finale of the #1 New York Times bestselling Reckoners trilogy that began with <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i>.<br /><br />Brandon Sanderson was born in 1975 in Lincoln, Nebraska. As a child Brandon enjoyed reading, but he lost interest in the types of titles often suggested to him, and by junior high he never cracked a book if he could help it. This changed when an eighth grade teacher gave him <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176268.Dragonsbane" title="Dragonsbane" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsbane</a>
</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10333.Barbara_Hambly" title="Barbara Hambly" rel="nofollow noopener">Barbara Hambly</a>.<br /><br />Brandon was working on his thirteenth novel when Moshe Feder at Tor Books bought the sixth he had written. Tor has published <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68427.Elantris" title="Elantris" rel="nofollow noopener">Elantris</a>,</i> the Mistborn trilogy and its followup <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10803121.The_Alloy_of_Law" title="The Alloy of Law" rel="nofollow noopener">The Alloy of Law</a>,</i> <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1268479.Warbreaker" title="Warbreaker" rel="nofollow noopener">Warbreaker</a>,</i> and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7235533.The_Way_of_Kings" title="The Way of Kings" rel="nofollow noopener">The Way of Kings</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11543195.Words_of_Radiance" title="Words of Radiance" rel="nofollow noopener">Words of Radiance</a>,</i> the first two in the planned ten-volume series The Stormlight Archive. He was chosen to complete <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6252.Robert_Jordan" title="Robert Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Jordan</a>’s Wheel of Time series; 2009’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.The_Gathering_Storm" title="The Gathering Storm" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gathering Storm</a>
</i> and 2010’s <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8253920.Towers_of_Midnight" title="Towers of Midnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Towers of Midnight</a>
</i> were followed by the final book in the series, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1166599.A_Memory_of_Light" title="A Memory of Light" rel="nofollow noopener">A Memory of Light</a>,</i> in January 2013. Four books in his middle-grade <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/623976.Alcatraz_vs__the_Evil_Librarians" title="Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians" rel="nofollow noopener">Alcatraz vs. the Evil Librarians</a>
</i> series have been released in new editions by Starscape, and his novella <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12796771.Infinity_Blade_Awakening" title="Infinity Blade Awakening" rel="nofollow noopener">Infinity Blade Awakening</a>
</i> was an ebook bestseller for Epic Games accompanying their acclaimed <i>Infinity Blade</i> iOS video game series. Two more novellas, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13452375.Legion" title="Legion" rel="nofollow noopener">Legion</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13578175.The_Emperor_s_Soul" title="The Emperor’s Soul" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor’s Soul</a>,</i> were released by Subterranean Press and Tachyon Publications in 2012, and 2013 brought two young adult novels, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10137823.The_Rithmatist" title="The Rithmatist" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rithmatist</a>
</i> from Tor and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17182126.Steelheart" title="Steelheart" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a>
</i> from Delacorte.<br /><br />The only author to make the short list for the David Gemmell Legend Award six times in four years, Brandon won that award in 2011 for <i>The Way of Kings</i>. <i>The Emperor’s Soul</i> won the 2013 Hugo Award for Best Novella. He has appeared on the <i>New York Times</i> Best-Seller List multiple times, with five novels hitting the #1 spot.<br /><br />Currently living in Utah with his wife and children, Brandon teaches creative writing at Brigham Young University.</span>
